</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Open-source model</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source">Open source</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the general production and development model. For its application to software, see <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_development_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source software development model">Open-source software development model</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Open_source_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Open source (disambiguation)">Open source (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambox_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Ambox question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ambox_question.svg/40px-Ambox_question.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ambox_question.svg/60px-Ambox_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ambox_question.svg/80px-Ambox_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>possibly contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Synthesis_of_published_material_that_advances_a_position" title="Wikipedia:No original research">previously unpublished synthesis</a> of published material that conveys ideas not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">attributable</a> to the original sources.</b> <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Open-source_model#.23" title="Talk:Open-source model">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>open-source model</b> is a decentralized <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">development model</a> that encourages <a href="/wiki/Open_collaboration" title="Open collaboration">open collaboration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-doi.org_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doi.org-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> A main principle of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_development" title="Open-source software development">open-source software development</a> is <a href="/wiki/Peer_production" title="Peer production">peer production</a>, with products such as source code, <a href="/wiki/Blueprints" class="mw-redirect" title="Blueprints">blueprints</a>, and documentation freely available to the public. The <a href="/wiki/Open-source_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source movement">open-source movement</a> in software began as a response to the limitations of proprietary code. The model is used for projects such as in <a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source appropriate technologies">open-source appropriate technologies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and open-source drug discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Open source promotes universal access via an <a href="/wiki/Open-source_license" title="Open-source license">open-source</a> or <a href="/wiki/Free_license" title="Free license">free license</a> to a product's design or blueprint, and universal redistribution of that design or blueprint.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Before the phrase <i>open source</i> became widely adopted, developers and producers used a variety of other terms. <i>Open source</i> gained hold with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_movement" title="Open-source software movement">open-source software movement</a> arose to clarify <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Licensing" class="mw-redirect" title="Licensing">licensing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain</a>, and consumer issues.</p>
<p>Generally, open source refers to a <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">computer program</a> in which the <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> is available to the general public for use and/or modification from its original design. Open-source code is meant to be a collaborative effort, where programmers improve upon the source code and share the changes within the community. Code is released under the terms of a <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">software license</a>. Depending on the license terms, others may then download, modify, and publish their version (fork) back to the community.</p>
<p>Many large formal institutions have sprung up to support the development of the open-source movement, including the <a href="/wiki/Apache_Software_Foundation" title="Apache Software Foundation">Apache Software Foundation</a>, which supports community projects such as the open-source framework <a href="/wiki/Apache_Hadoop" title="Apache Hadoop">Apache Hadoop</a> and the open-source <a href="/wiki/HTTP" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP">HTTP</a> server <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache HTTP</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_free_and_open-source_software" title="History of free and open-source software">History of free and open-source software</a></div>
<p>The sharing of technical information predates the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> and the personal computer considerably. For instance, in the early years of automobile development a group of capital <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopolists</a> owned the rights to a <a href="/wiki/2_cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="2 cycle">2-cycle</a> gasoline engine patent originally filed by <a href="/wiki/George_B._Selden" title="George B. Selden">George B. Selden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-9">[9]</a></sup> By controlling this patent, they were able to monopolize the industry and force car manufacturers to adhere to their demands, or risk a lawsuit.</p>
<p>In 1911, independent automaker <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> won a challenge to the Selden patent. The result was that the Selden patent became virtually worthless and a new association (which would eventually become the <a href="/wiki/Motor_Vehicle_Manufacturers_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor Vehicle Manufacturers Association">Motor Vehicle Manufacturers Association</a>) was formed.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-9">[9]</a></sup> The new association instituted a cross-licensing agreement among all US auto manufacturers: although each company would develop technology and file patents, these patents were shared openly and without the exchange of money among all the manufacturers.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-9">[9]</a></sup> By the time the US entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, 92 Ford patents and 515 patents from other companies were being shared among these manufacturers, without any exchange of money (or lawsuits).<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early instances of the free sharing of source code include <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s source releases of its <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a> and other programs in the 1950s and 1960s, and the <a href="/wiki/SHARE_(computing)" title="SHARE (computing)">SHARE</a> user group that formed to facilitate the exchange of software.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated172_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated172-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-11">[11]</a></sup> Beginning in the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/ARPANET" title="ARPANET">ARPANET</a> researchers used an open "<a href="/wiki/Request_for_Comments" title="Request for Comments">Request for Comments</a>" (RFC) process to encourage feedback in early telecommunication network protocols. This led to the birth of the early Internet in 1969.</p>
<p>The sharing of source code on the Internet began when the Internet was relatively primitive, with software distributed via <a href="/wiki/UUCP" title="UUCP">UUCP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">Usenet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" title="Internet Relay Chat">IRC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gopher_(protocol)" title="Gopher (protocol)">Gopher</a>. <a href="/wiki/BSD" class="mw-redirect" title="BSD">BSD</a>, for example, was first widely distributed by posts to comp.os.linux on the Usenet, which is also where its development was discussed. <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> followed in this model.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_source_as_a_term">Open source as a term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Open source as a term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term "open source" was first proposed by a group of people in the <a href="/wiki/Free_software_movement" title="Free software movement">free software movement</a> who were critical of the political agenda and moral philosophy implied in the term "free software" and sought to reframe the discourse to reflect a more commercially minded position.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In addition, the ambiguity of the term "free software" was seen as discouraging business adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infoworld1983_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoworld1983-14">[14]</a></sup> The group included <a href="/wiki/Christine_Peterson" title="Christine Peterson">Christine Peterson</a>, Todd Anderson, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Augustin" title="Larry Augustin">Larry Augustin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Hall_(programmer)" title="Jon Hall (programmer)">Jon Hall</a>, Sam Ockman, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tiemann" title="Michael Tiemann">Michael Tiemann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_S._Raymond" title="Eric S. Raymond">Eric S. Raymond</a>. Peterson suggested "open source" at a meeting<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-15">[15]</a></sup> held at <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a>, in reaction to <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Netscape Communications Corporation">Netscape</a>'s announcement in January 1998 of a source code release for <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Navigator" title="Netscape Navigator">Navigator</a>. <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">Linus Torvalds</a> gave his support the following day, and Phil Hughes backed the term in <i><a href="/wiki/Linux_Journal" title="Linux Journal">Linux Journal</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a>, the founder of the free software movement, initially seemed to adopt the term, but later changed his mind.<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rmsdissent_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmsdissent-16">[16]</a></sup> Netscape released its source code under the <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Public_License" title="Netscape Public License">Netscape Public License</a> and later under the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Public_License" title="Mozilla Public License">Mozilla Public License</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Muffatto000_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muffatto000-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Raymond was especially active in the effort to popularize the new term. He made the first public call to the free software community to adopt it in February 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-raymondCall_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raymondCall-18">[18]</a></sup> Shortly after, he founded The <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Initiative" title="Open Source Initiative">Open Source Initiative</a> in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Perens" title="Bruce Perens">Bruce Perens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term gained further visibility through an event organized in April 1998 by technology publisher <a href="/wiki/Tim_O%27Reilly" title="Tim O'Reilly">Tim O'Reilly</a>. Originally titled the "Freeware Summit" and later known as the "Open Source Summit",<sup id="cite_ref-opensourcesummit_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opensourcesummit-19">[19]</a></sup> the event was attended by the leaders of many of the most important free and open-source projects, including Linus Torvalds, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Wall" title="Larry Wall">Larry Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Behlendorf" title="Brian Behlendorf">Brian Behlendorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Allman" title="Eric Allman">Eric Allman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guido_van_Rossum" title="Guido van Rossum">Guido van Rossum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tiemann" title="Michael Tiemann">Michael Tiemann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Vixie" title="Paul Vixie">Paul Vixie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Zawinski" title="Jamie Zawinski">Jamie Zawinski</a>, and Eric Raymond. At that meeting, alternatives to the term "free software" were discussed. Tiemann argued for "sourceware" as a new term, while Raymond argued for "open source". The assembled developers took a vote, and the winner was announced at a press conference the same evening.<sup id="cite_ref-opensourcesummit_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opensourcesummit-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Open source" has never managed to entirely supersede the older term "free software", giving rise to the combined term <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> (FOSS).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_economics" title="Open-source economics">Open-source economics</a></div>
<p>Some economists agree that open-source is an <a href="/wiki/Information_good" title="Information good">information good</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> or "knowledge good" with original work involving a significant amount of time, money, and effort. The cost of reproducing the work is low enough that additional users may be added at zero or near zero cost&#160;– this is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Marginal_cost" title="Marginal cost">marginal cost</a> of a product. <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">Copyright</a> creates a monopoly so the price charged to consumers can be significantly higher than the marginal cost of production. This allows the author to recoup the cost of making the original work. Copyright thus creates access costs for consumers who value the work more than the marginal cost but less than the initial production cost. Access costs also pose problems for authors who wish to create a <a href="/wiki/Derivative_work" title="Derivative work">derivative work</a>—such as a copy of a software program modified to fix a bug or add a feature, or a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> of a song—but are unable or unwilling to pay the copyright holder for the right to do so.</p>
<p>Being organized as effectively a "<a href="/wiki/Consumers%27_cooperative" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumers' cooperative">consumers' cooperative</a>", open source eliminates some of the access costs of consumers and creators of derivative works by reducing the restrictions of copyright. Basic economic theory predicts that lower costs would lead to higher consumption and also more frequent creation of derivative works. Organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> host websites where individuals can file for alternative "licenses", or levels of restriction, for their works.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> These self-made protections free the general society of the costs of policing copyright infringement.</p>
<p>Others argue that since consumers do not pay for their copies, creators are unable to recoup the initial cost of production and thus have little economic incentive to create in the first place. By this argument, consumers would lose out because some of the goods they would otherwise purchase would not be available. In practice, content producers can choose whether to adopt a proprietary license and charge for copies, or an open license. Some goods which require large amounts of professional research and development, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a> (which depends largely on <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a>, not copyright for intellectual property protection) are almost exclusively proprietary, although increasingly sophisticated technologies are being developed on open-source principles.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is evidence that open-source development creates enormous value.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> For example, in the context of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a> design, digital designs are shared for free and anyone with access to digital manufacturing technologies (e.g. <a href="/wiki/RepRap" class="mw-redirect" title="RepRap">RepRap</a> 3D printers) can replicate the product for the cost of materials.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The original sharer may receive feedback and potentially improvements on the original design from the <a href="/wiki/Peer_production" title="Peer production">peer production</a> community.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Licensing_alternatives">Licensing alternatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Licensing alternatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Business_models_for_open-source_software" title="Business models for open-source software">Business models for open-source software</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Smart_phones.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/Smart_phones.jpg/220px-Smart_phones.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/Smart_phones.jpg/330px-Smart_phones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/Smart_phones.jpg/440px-Smart_phones.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Smart_phones.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Google Android operating system</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alternative arrangements have also been shown to result in good creation outside of the proprietary license model. Examples include:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Creation for its own sake – For example, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> editors add content for recreation. Artists have a drive to create. Both communities benefit from free starting material.</li>
<li>Voluntary after-the-fact donations – used by <a href="/wiki/Shareware" title="Shareware">shareware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Street_performer" class="mw-redirect" title="Street performer">street performers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcasting</a> in the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Patron – For example, <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">open access</a> publishing relies on institutional and government funding of research faculty, who also have a professional incentive to publish for reputation and career advancement. Works of the U.S. federal government are automatically released into the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Freemium" title="Freemium">Freemium</a> – Give away a limited version for free and charge for a premium version (potentially using a <a href="/wiki/Dual_license" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual license">dual license</a>).</li>
<li>Give away the product and charge something related – Charge for support of open-source <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_software" title="Enterprise software">enterprise software</a>, give away music but charge for concert admission.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Give away work in order to gain market share – Used by artists, in corporate software to spoil a dominant competitor (for example in the <a href="/wiki/Browser_wars" title="Browser wars">browser wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Android_operating_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Android operating system">Android operating system</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>For own use – Businesses or individual software developers often create software to solve a problem, bearing the full cost of initial creation. They will then open source the solution, and benefit from the improvements others make for their own needs. Communalizing the maintenance burden distributes the cost across more users; <a href="/wiki/Free_rider_problem" title="Free rider problem">free riders</a> can also benefit without undermining the creation process.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_source_applications">Open source applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Open source applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/250px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png" width="250" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/375px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/500px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="1646" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Open-source model application domains</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Social and political views have been affected by the growth of the concept of open source. Advocates in one field often support the expansion of open source in other fields. But <a href="/wiki/Eric_Raymond" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Raymond">Eric Raymond</a> and other founders of the <a href="/wiki/Open-source_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source movement">open-source movement</a> have sometimes publicly argued against speculation about applications outside software, saying that strong arguments for software openness should not be weakened by overreaching into areas where the story may be less compelling. The broader impact of the open-source movement, and the extent of its role in the development of new information sharing procedures, remain to be seen.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Open-source_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source movement">open-source movement</a> has inspired increased <a href="/wiki/Transparency_(humanities)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transparency (humanities)">transparency</a> and liberty in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research, for example by <a href="/wiki/CAMBIA" title="CAMBIA">CAMBIA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Even the research methodologies themselves can benefit from the application of open-source principles.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It has also given rise to the rapidly-expanding <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a> movement.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_software">Computer software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Computer software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open_source_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Free and open source software">Free and open source software</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blender_2.59_Startup.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Blender_2.59_Startup.png/220px-Blender_2.59_Startup.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Blender_2.59_Startup.png/330px-Blender_2.59_Startup.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Blender_2.59_Startup.png/440px-Blender_2.59_Startup.png 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blender_2.59_Startup.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Blender_(software)" title="Blender (software)">Blender</a> is an open-source 3D graphics editor.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/150px-Android_6.0-en.png" width="150" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/225px-Android_6.0-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/300px-Android_6.0-en.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, the most popular mobile operating system (as of Nov 2012)<sup id="cite_ref-idcQ3_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idcQ3-27">[27]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">Open-source software</a> is software whose source code is published and made available to the public, enabling anyone to copy, modify and redistribute the source code without paying royalties or fees.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Open-source code can evolve through community cooperation. These communities are composed of individual programmers as well as large companies. Some of the individual programmers who start an open-source project may end up establishing companies offering products or services incorporating open-source programs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Examples of open-source software products are:<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics">Electronics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Electronics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Open-source-hardware-logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Open-source-hardware-logo.svg/100px-Open-source-hardware-logo.svg.png" width="100" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Open-source-hardware-logo.svg/150px-Open-source-hardware-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Open-source-hardware-logo.svg/200px-Open-source-hardware-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="538" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Open-source-hardware-logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Hardware" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Source Hardware">Open Source Hardware</a> logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">Open-source hardware</a> is hardware whose initial specification, usually in a software format, are published and made available to the public, enabling anyone to copy, modify and redistribute the hardware and source code without paying royalties or fees. Open-source hardware evolves through community cooperation. These communities are composed of individual hardware/software developers, hobbyists, as well as very large companies. Examples of open-source hardware initiatives are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Openmoko" title="Openmoko">Openmoko</a>: a family of open-source <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phones</a>, including the hardware specification and the <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenRISC" title="OpenRISC">OpenRISC</a>: an open-source microprocessor family, with architecture specification licensed under <a href="/wiki/GNU_GPL" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU GPL">GNU GPL</a> and implementation under <a href="/wiki/LGPL" class="mw-redirect" title="LGPL">LGPL</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>'s <a href="/wiki/OpenSPARC" title="OpenSPARC">OpenSPARC</a> T1 Multicore processor. Sun has released it under GPL.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arduino" title="Arduino">Arduino</a>, a microcontroller platform for hobbyists, artists and designers.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=GizmoSphere&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GizmoSphere (page does not exist)">GizmoSphere</a>, an open-source development platform for the embedded design community; the site includes code downloads and hardware schematics along with free user guides, spec sheets and other documentation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simputer" title="Simputer">Simputer</a>, an open hardware <a href="/wiki/Handheld_computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Handheld computer">handheld computer</a>, designed in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> for use in environments where computing devices such as personal computers are deemed inappropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LEON" title="LEON">LEON</a>: A family of open-source microprocessors distributed in a library with peripheral <a href="/wiki/IP_core" class="mw-redirect" title="IP core">IP cores</a>, open <a href="/wiki/SPARC" title="SPARC">SPARC</a> V8 specification, implementation available under <a href="/wiki/GNU_GPL" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU GPL">GNU GPL</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tinkerforge" title="Tinkerforge">Tinkerforge</a>: A system of open-source stackable microcontroller building blocks. Allows to control motors and read out sensors with the programming languages C, C++, C#, Object Pascal, Java, PHP, Python and Ruby over a USB or Wifi connection on Windows, Linux and Mac OS X. All of the hardware is licensed under <a href="/wiki/CERN_Open_Hardware_License" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN Open Hardware License">CERN OHL</a> (CERN Open Hardware License).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Compute_Project" title="Open Compute Project">Open Compute Project</a>: designs for computer data center including power supply, Intel motherboard, AMD motherboard, chassis, racks, battery cabinet, and aspects of electrical and mechanical design.<sup id="cite_ref-OpenComputeProj_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenComputeProj-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lasersaur" title="Lasersaur">Lasersaur</a>, an open-source <a href="/wiki/Laser_cutter" class="mw-redirect" title="Laser cutter">laser cutter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_beverages">Food and beverages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Food and beverages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Voresol_label_medium.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/100px-Voresol_label_medium.png" width="100" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/150px-Voresol_label_medium.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/200px-Voresol_label_medium.png 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="559" /></a>
