<a href="/wiki/Vores_%C3%98l" class="mw-redirect" title="Vores Øl">Vores Øl - An Open Source Beer</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dakota_Meyer" title="Dakota Meyer">Dakota Meyer</a> drinking <a href="/wiki/White_House_Honey_Ale" title="White House Honey Ale">White House Honey Ale</a> in 2011. The recipe is available for free.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some publishers of <a href="/wiki/Open-access" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-access">open-access</a> journals have argued that <a href="/wiki/Open_data" title="Open data">data</a> from <a href="/wiki/Food_science" title="Food science">food science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a> studies should be freely available to aid <a href="/wiki/Reproducibility" title="Reproducibility">reproducibility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> A number of people have published creative commons licensed recipe books.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_cola" title="Open-source cola">Open-source colas</a> – cola soft drinks, similar to <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>, whose recipe is open source and developed by volunteers. The taste is said to be comparable to that of the standard beverages. Most corporations producing beverages hold their formulas as closely guarded secrets.<sup id="cite_ref-octavio1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-octavio1-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Free_Beer" title="Free Beer">Free Beer</a> (originally <i>Vores Øl</i>) – is an open-source beer created by students at the <a href="/wiki/IT_University_of_Copenhagen" title="IT University of Copenhagen">IT-University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Superflex" title="Superflex">Superflex</a>, an artist collective, to illustrate how open-source concepts might be applied outside the digital world.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2002, the beer company <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brewtopia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brewtopia (page does not exist)">Brewtopia</a> in Australia started an open-source brewery and invited the general population to be involved in the development and ownership of the brewery, and to vote on the development of every aspect of its beer, Blowfly, and its road to market. In return for their feedback and input, individuals received shares in the company, which is now publicly traded on a stock exchange in Australia. The company has always adhered to its open-source roots and is the only beer company in the world that allows the public to design, customise and develop its own beers online.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_content">Digital content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Digital content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Knowledge_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Open_Knowledge_logo.png/100px-Open_Knowledge_logo.png" width="100" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Open_Knowledge_logo.png/150px-Open_Knowledge_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Open_Knowledge_logo.png/200px-Open_Knowledge_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="910" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Knowledge_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Open_Knowledge_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Knowledge Foundation">Open Knowledge Foundation</a> logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://wikimediafoundation.org/wiki/Our_projects">Open-content projects organized by the Wikimedia Foundation</a> – Sites such as Wikipedia and Wiktionary have embraced the open-content <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> content licenses. These licenses were designed to adhere to principles similar to various open-source software development licenses. Many of these licenses ensure that content remains free for re-use, that source documents are made readily available to interested parties, and that changes to content are accepted easily back into the system. Important sites embracing open-source-like ideals are <a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a>, both of which post many books on which the copyright has expired and are thus in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>, ensuring that anyone has free, unlimited access to that content.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SketchUp_3D_Warehouse_screen_shot.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/30/SketchUp_3D_Warehouse_screen_shot.png/220px-SketchUp_3D_Warehouse_screen_shot.png" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/30/SketchUp_3D_Warehouse_screen_shot.png 1.5x" data-file-width="273" data-file-height="364" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SketchUp_3D_Warehouse_screen_shot.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
SketchUp's open-source 3D Warehouse library</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_ICEcat" class="mw-redirect" title="Open ICEcat">Open ICEcat</a> is an open catalog for the IT, CE and Lighting sectors with product data-sheets based on <a href="/wiki/Open_Content_License" title="Open Content License">Open Content License</a> agreement. The digital content are distributed in XML and URL formats.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google_Sketchup" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Sketchup">Google Sketchup</a>'s <a href="/wiki/3D_Warehouse" title="3D Warehouse">3D Warehouse</a> is an open-source design community centered around the use of proprietary software that's free.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_Stratford_Campus" title="University of Waterloo Stratford Campus">University of Waterloo Stratford Campus</a> invites students every year to use its three-storey Christie <a href="/wiki/MicroTiles" title="MicroTiles">MicroTiles</a> wall as a digital canvas for their creative work.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicine">Medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Pharmaceuticals – There have been several proposals for open-source pharmaceutical development,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> which led to the establishment of the Tropical Disease Initiative<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and the Open Source Drug Discovery for Malaria Consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>Genomics – The term "open-source genomics" refers to the combination of rapid release of sequence data (especially raw reads) and crowdsourced analyses from bioinformaticians around the world that characterised the analysis of the <a href="/wiki/2011_E._coli_O104:H4_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 E. coli O104:H4 outbreak">2011 E. coli O104:H4 outbreak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenEMR" title="OpenEMR">OpenEMR</a> – OpenEMR is an ONC-ATB Ambulatory EHR 2011-2012 certified electronic health records and medical practice management application. It features fully integrated electronic health, records, practice management, scheduling, electronic billing, and is the base for many EHR programs. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.open-emr.org/">http://www.open-emr.org/</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_engineering">Science and engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Science and engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg/100px-Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg.png" width="100" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg/150px-Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg/200px-Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">Open access</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Research – The <a href="/wiki/Science_Commons" title="Science Commons">Science Commons</a> was created as an alternative to the expensive legal costs of sharing and reusing scientific works in journals etc.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>Research – <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Open_Source_Science_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Open Source Science Project (page does not exist)">The Open Source Science Project</a> was created to increase the ability for students to participate in the research process by providing them access to microfunding&#160;– which, in turn, offers non-researchers the opportunity to directly invest, and follow, cutting-edge scientific research. All data and methodology is subsequently published in an openly accessible manner under a Creative Commons fair use license.</li>
<li>Research – <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Solar_Outdoors_Test_Field" title="The Open Solar Outdoors Test Field">The Open Solar Outdoors Test Field</a> (OSOTF)<sup id="cite_ref-osotf_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osotf-51">[51]</a></sup> is a grid-connected <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> test system, which continuously monitors the output of a number of photovoltaic modules and correlates their performance to a long list of highly accurate meteorological readings. The OSOTF is organized under open-source principles – All data and analysis is to be made freely available to the entire photovoltaic community and the general public.<sup id="cite_ref-osotf_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osotf-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>Engineering – <a href="/wiki/Hyperloop" title="Hyperloop">Hyperloop</a>, a form of high-speed transport proposed by entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, which he describes as "an elevated, reduced-pressure tube that contains pressurized capsules driven within the tube by a number of linear electric motors".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>Construction – <a href="/wiki/WikiHouse" title="WikiHouse">WikiHouse</a> is an open-source project for designing and building <a href="/wiki/House" title="House">houses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LaBarre_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaBarre-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kingsley_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingsley-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li>Energy research - The <a href="/wiki/Open_Energy_Modelling_Initiative" title="Open Energy Modelling Initiative">Open Energy Modelling Initiative</a> promotes open-source models and open data in energy research and policy advice.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Robotics">Robotics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Robotics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_robotics" title="Open-source robotics">Open-source robotics</a></div>
<p>An open-source robot is a <a href="/wiki/Robot" title="Robot">robot</a> whose blueprints, schematics, and/or source code are released under an open-source model.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.opentripplanner.org/">Open Trip Planner</a> - this code base is growing rapidly, with adoption in Portland, New York, The Netherlands and Helsinki.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.travelspirit.io">TravelSpirit</a> – a greater level of 'super-architecture' ambition, to bring a range of open source projects together, in order to deliver 'Mobility as a Service'</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eyewear" title="Eyewear">Eyewear</a> – In June 2013, an open-source eyewear brand, Botho, has started trading under the UK based Open Optics Ltd company.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/200px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg" width="200" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/300px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/400px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="590" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/VIA_OpenBook" title="VIA OpenBook">VIA OpenBook</a> is an open-source hardware laptop reference design.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Open-source principles can be applied to technical areas such as digital communication protocols and data storage formats.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_design" title="Open design">Open design</a> – which involves applying open-source methodologies to the design of artifacts and systems in the physical world. It is very nascent but has huge potential.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source appropriate technology">Open-source-appropriate technology</a> (OSAT) refers to technologies that are designed in the same fashion as <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-buitenhuis_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buitenhuis-58">[58]</a></sup> These technologies must be "<a href="/wiki/Appropriate_technology" title="Appropriate technology">appropriate technology</a>" (AT) – meaning technology that is designed with special consideration to the environmental, ethical, cultural, social, political, and economic aspects of the community it is intended for. An example of this application is the use of open-source 3D printers like the <a href="/wiki/RepRap" class="mw-redirect" title="RepRap">RepRap</a> to manufacture appropriate technology.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-Source_Learning&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open-Source Learning (page does not exist)">Teaching</a> – which involves applying the concepts of open source to instruction using a shared web space as a platform to improve upon learning, organizational, and management challenges. An example of an Open-source courseware is the Java Education &amp; Development Initiative (JEDI).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Other examples include <a href="/wiki/Khan_Academy" title="Khan Academy">Khan Academy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikiversity" title="Wikiversity">wikiversity</a>. At the university level, the use of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source appropriate technology">open-source-appropriate technology</a> classroom projects has been shown to be successful in forging the connection between science/engineering and social benefit:<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> This approach has the potential to use university students' access to resources and testing equipment in furthering the development of <a href="/wiki/Appropriate_technology" title="Appropriate technology">appropriate technology</a>. Similarly OSAT has been used as a tool for improving <a href="/wiki/Service_learning" class="mw-redirect" title="Service learning">service learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li>There are few examples of business information (methodologies, advice, guidance, practices) using the open-source model, although this is another case where the potential is enormous. <a href="/wiki/ITIL" title="ITIL">ITIL</a> is close to open source. It uses the Cathedral model (no mechanism exists for user contribution) and the content must be bought for a fee that is small by business consulting standards (hundreds of British pounds). Various checklists are published by government, banks or accounting firms.</li>
<li>An open-source group emerged in 2012 that is attempting to design a firearm that may be downloaded from the internet and "printed" on a <a href="/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">3D Printer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-f20120823_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f20120823-64">[64]</a></sup> Calling itself <a href="/wiki/Defense_Distributed" title="Defense Distributed">Defense Distributed</a>, the group wants to facilitate "a working plastic gun that could be downloaded and reproduced by anybody with a 3D printer".<sup id="cite_ref-pcm20120824_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcm20120824-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-disputed" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:System-search.svg" class="image"><img alt="System-search.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/45px-System-search.svg.png" width="45" height="45" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/68px-System-search.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/90px-System-search.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b>factual accuracy is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">disputed</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help to ensure that disputed statements are <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliably sourced</a>. See the relevant discussion on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Open-source_model#Dispute" title="Talk:Open-source model">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(December 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The rise of open-source culture in the 20th century resulted from a growing tension between creative practices that involve require access to content that is often <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyrighted</a>, and restrictive intellectual property laws and policies governing access to copyrighted content. The two main ways in which intellectual property laws became more restrictive in the 20th century were extensions to the term of copyright (particularly in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>) and penalties, such as those articulated in the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Millennium_Copyright_Act" title="Digital Millennium Copyright Act">Digital Millennium Copyright Act</a> (DMCA), placed on attempts to circumvent anti-piracy technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-copyright1998_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-copyright1998-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although artistic appropriation is often permitted under <a href="/wiki/Fair_use" title="Fair use">fair-use</a> doctrines, the complexity and ambiguity of these doctrines creates an atmosphere of uncertainty among cultural practitioners. Also, the protective actions of copyright owners create what some call a "<a href="/wiki/Chilling_effect_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilling effect (term)">chilling effect</a>" among cultural practitioners.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The idea of an "open-source" culture runs parallel to "<a href="/wiki/Free_Culture_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Culture movement">Free Culture</a>," but is substantively different. <i>Free culture</i> is a term derived from the <a href="/wiki/Free_software_movement" title="Free software movement">free software movement</a>, and in contrast to that vision of culture, proponents of open-source culture (OSC) maintain that some intellectual property law needs to exist to protect cultural producers. Yet they propose a more nuanced position than corporations have traditionally sought. Instead of seeing intellectual property law as an expression of instrumental rules intended to uphold either natural rights or desirable outcomes, an argument for OSC takes into account diverse goods (as in "the Good life") and ends.</p>
<p>Sites such as <a href="/wiki/CcMixter" title="CcMixter">ccMixter</a> offer up free web space for anyone willing to license their work under a <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> license. The resulting cultural product is then available to download free (generally accessible) to anyone with an Internet connection.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Older analog technologies such as the <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">telephone</a> or <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> have limitations on the kind of interaction users can have.</p>
<p>Through various technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> networks and <a href="/wiki/Blogs" class="mw-redirect" title="Blogs">blogs</a>, cultural producers can take advantage of vast <a href="/wiki/Social_networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Social networks">social networks</a> to distribute their products. As opposed to traditional media distribution, redistributing digital media on the Internet can be virtually costless. Technologies such as <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_(protocol)" class="mw-redirect" title="BitTorrent (protocol)">BitTorrent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gnutella" title="Gnutella">Gnutella</a> take advantage of various characteristics of the Internet protocol (<a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a>) in an attempt to totally decentralize file distribution.</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_movement" title="Open-source software movement">Open-source software movement</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_politics" class="mw-redirect" title="Open politics">Open politics</a> (sometimes known as <i>Open-source politics</i>) is a political process that uses Internet technologies such as blogs, email and polling to provide for a rapid feedback mechanism between political organizations and their supporters. There is also an alternative conception of the term <i>Open-source politics</i> which relates to the development of public policy under a set of rules and processes similar to the open-source software movement.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_governance" title="Open-source governance">Open-source governance</a> is similar to open-source politics, but it applies more to the democratic process and promotes the freedom of information.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/South_Korean_government" class="mw-redirect" title="South Korean government">South Korean government</a> wants to increase its use of free and open-source software, in order to decrease its dependence on proprietary software solutions. It plans to make open standards a requirement, to allow the government to choose between multiple operating systems and web browsers. Korea's Ministry of Science, ICT &amp; Future Planning is also preparing ten pilots on using open-source software distributions.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethics">Ethics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Open-source ethics is split into two strands:</p>
<ul>
<li>Open-source ethics as an ethical school – Charles Ess and David Berry are researching whether ethics can learn anything from an open-source approach. Ess famously even defined the AoIR Research Guidelines as an example of open-source ethics.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>Open-source ethics as a professional body of rules – This is based principally on the computer ethics school, studying the questions of ethics and professionalism in the computer industry in general and software development in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Irish philosopher Richard Kearney has used the term "open-source Hinduism" to refer to the way historical figures such as Mohandas Gandhi and Swami Vivekananda worked upon this ancient tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_journalism" title="Open-source journalism">Open-source journalism</a> formerly referred to the standard journalistic techniques of news gathering and fact checking, reflecting <i><a href="/wiki/Open-source_intelligence" title="Open-source intelligence">open-source intelligence</a></i> a similar term used in military intelligence circles. Now, <i>open-source journalism</i> commonly refers to forms of innovative publishing of <a href="/wiki/Online_journalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Online journalism">online journalism</a>, rather than the sourcing of news stories by a professional journalist. In the December 25, 2006 issue of TIME magazine this is referred to as <a href="/wiki/User_generated_content" class="mw-redirect" title="User generated content">user created content</a> and listed alongside more traditional open-source projects such as <a href="/wiki/OpenSolaris" title="OpenSolaris">OpenSolaris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">Weblogs</a>, or blogs, are another significant platform for open-source culture. Blogs consist of periodic, reverse chronologically ordered posts, using a technology that makes webpages easily updatable with no understanding of design, code, or <a href="/wiki/File_transfer" title="File transfer">file transfer</a> required. While corporations, political campaigns and other formal institutions have begun using these tools to distribute information, many blogs are used by individuals for personal expression, political organizing, and socializing. Some, such as <a href="/wiki/LiveJournal" title="LiveJournal">LiveJournal</a> or <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a>, utilize open-source software that is open to the public and can be modified by users to fit their own tastes. Whether the code is open or not, this format represents a nimble tool for people to borrow and re-present culture; whereas traditional websites made the illegal reproduction of culture difficult to regulate, the mutability of blogs makes "open sourcing" even more uncontrollable since it allows a larger portion of the population to replicate material more quickly in the public sphere.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Messageboards" class="mw-redirect" title="Messageboards">Messageboards</a> are another platform for open-source culture. Messageboards (also known as discussion boards or forums), are places online where people with similar interests can congregate and post messages for the community to read and respond to. Messageboards sometimes have moderators who enforce community standards of etiquette such as banning users who are <a href="/wiki/Spamming" title="Spamming">spammers</a>. Other common board features are private messages (where users can send messages to one another) as well as chat (a way to have a real time conversation online) and image uploading. Some messageboards use <a href="/wiki/PhpBB" title="PhpBB">phpBB</a>, which is a free open-source package. Where blogs are more about individual expression and tend to revolve around their authors, messageboards are about creating a conversation amongst its users where information can be shared freely and quickly. Messageboards are a way to remove intermediaries from everyday life—for instance, instead of relying on commercials and other forms of advertising, one can ask other users for frank reviews of a product, movie or CD. By removing the cultural middlemen, messageboards help speed the flow of information and exchange of ideas.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Open_format" title="Open format">open</a> <a href="/wiki/Document_file_format" title="Document file format">document file format</a> for saving and exchanging editable office documents such as text documents (including memos, reports, and books), <a href="/wiki/Spreadsheet" title="Spreadsheet">spreadsheets</a>, charts, and presentations. Organizations and individuals that store their data in an open format such as OpenDocument avoid being <a href="/wiki/Vendor_lock-in" title="Vendor lock-in">locked into</a> a single software vendor, leaving them free to switch software if their current vendor goes out of business, raises their prices, changes their software, or changes their <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">licensing</a> terms to something less favorable.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_film" title="Open-source film">Open-source movie production</a> is either an open call system in which a changing crew and cast collaborate in movie production, a system in which the end result is made available for re-use by others or in which exclusively open-source products are used in the production. The 2006 movie <a href="/wiki/Elephants_Dream" title="Elephants Dream">Elephants Dream</a> is said to be the "world's first open movie",<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> created entirely using <a href="/wiki/Open-source_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source technology">open-source technology</a>.</p>
<p>An open-source documentary film has a production process allowing the open contributions of archival material <a href="/wiki/Footage" title="Footage">footage</a>, and other filmic elements, both in unedited and edited form, similar to crowdsourcing. By doing so, on-line contributors become part of the process of creating the film, helping to influence the editorial and visual material to be used in the documentary, as well as its thematic development. The first open-source documentary film is the non-profit "<a href="/wiki/The_American_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="The American Revolution">The American Revolution</a>", which went into development in 2006, and will examine the role media played in the cultural, social and political changes from 1968 to 1974 through the story of radio station WBCN-FM in Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The film is being produced by Lichtenstein Creative Media and the non-profit Filmmakers Collaborative. Open Source Cinema is a website to create Basement Tapes, a feature documentary about copyright in the digital age, co-produced by the National Film Board of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Open-source_film" title="Open-source film">Open-source film-making</a> refers to a form of film-making that takes a method of idea formation from open-source software, but in this case the 'source' for a filmmaker is raw unedited footage rather than programming code. It can also refer to a method of film-making where the process of creation is 'open' i.e. a disparate group of contributors, at different times contribute to the final piece.</p>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-IPTV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open-IPTV (page does not exist)">Open-IPTV</a> is <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> that is not limited to one recording studio, production studio, or cast. Open-IPTV uses the Internet or other means to pool efforts and resources together to create an online community that all contributes to a show.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg/100px-Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg.png" width="100" height="67" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg/150px-Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg/200px-Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="567" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Open_Educational_Resources_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Open_Educational_Resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Educational Resources">Open Educational Resources</a> logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Within the academic community, there is discussion about expanding what could be called the "intellectual commons" (analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a>). Proponents of this view have hailed the <a href="/wiki/Connexions" class="mw-redirect" title="Connexions">Connexions</a> Project at <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">Rice University</a>, <a href="/wiki/MIT_OpenCourseWare" title="MIT OpenCourseWare">OpenCourseWare</a> project at <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Thacker" title="Eugene Thacker">Eugene Thacker</a>'s article on "open-source DNA", the "Open Source Cultural Database", <a href="/wiki/Salman_Khan_(educator)" class="mw-redirect" title="Salman Khan (educator)">Salman Khan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Khan_Academy" title="Khan Academy">Khan Academy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> as examples of applying open source outside the realm of computer software.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_curriculum" title="Open-source curriculum">Open-source curricula</a> are instructional resources whose digital source can be freely used, distributed and modified.</p>
<p>Another strand to the academic community is in the area of research. Many funded research projects produce software as part of their work. There is an increasing interest in making the outputs of such projects available under an open-source license. In the UK the <a href="/wiki/Jisc" title="Jisc">Joint Information Systems Committee (JISC)</a> has developed a policy on open-source software. JISC also funds a development service called <a href="/wiki/OSS_Watch" title="OSS Watch">OSS Watch</a> which acts as an advisory service for higher and further education institutions wishing to use, contribute to and develop open-source software.</p>
<p>On March 30, 2010, President Barack Obama signed the Health Care and Education Reconciliation Act, which included $2 billion over four years to fund the TAACCCT program, which is described as "the largest OER (open education resources) initiative in the world and uniquely focused on creating curricula in partnership with industry for credentials in vocational industry sectors like manufacturing, health, energy, transportation, and IT".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Innovation_communities">Innovation communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Innovation communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The principle of sharing pre-dates the open-source movement; for example, the free sharing of information has been institutionalized in the scientific enterprise since at least the 19th century. Open-source principles have always been part of the scientific community. The sociologist <a href="/wiki/Robert_K._Merton" title="Robert K. Merton">Robert K. Merton</a> described the four basic elements of the community—universalism (an international perspective), communalism (sharing information), disinterestedness (removing one's personal views from the scientific inquiry) and organized skepticism (requirements of proof and review) that accurately describe the scientific community today.</p>
<p>These principles are, in part, complemented by US law's focus on protecting expression and method but not the ideas themselves. There is also a tradition of publishing research results to the scientific community instead of keeping all such knowledge proprietary. One of the recent initiatives in scientific publishing has been <a href="/wiki/Open_access_(publishing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Open access (publishing)">open access</a>—the idea that research should be published in such a way that it is free and available to the public. There are currently many open access journals where the information is available free online, however most journals do charge a fee (either to users or libraries for access). The <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Open_Access_Initiative" title="Budapest Open Access Initiative">Budapest Open Access Initiative</a> is an international effort with the goal of making all research articles available free on the Internet.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> has recently proposed a policy on "Enhanced Public Access to NIH Research Information". This policy would provide a free, searchable resource of NIH-funded results to the public and with other international repositories six months after its initial publication. The NIH's move is an important one because there is significant amount of public funding in scientific research. Many of the questions have yet to be answered—the balancing of profit vs. public access, and ensuring that desirable standards and incentives do not diminish with a shift to open access.</p>
<p>Farmavita.Net is a community of pharmaceuticals executives that has recently proposed a new business model of open-source pharmaceuticals.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The project is targeted to development and sharing of know-how for manufacture of essential and life-saving medicines. It is mainly dedicated to the countries with less developed economies where local pharmaceutical research and development resources are insufficient for national needs. It will be limited to generic (off-patent) medicines with established use. By the definition, medicinal product have a "well-established use" if is used for at least 15 years, with recognized efficacy and an acceptable level of safety. In that event, the expensive clinical test and trial results could be replaced by appropriate scientific literature.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a> was an early contributor eventually donating all his inventions including the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_stove" title="Franklin stove">Franklin stove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bifocals" title="Bifocals">bifocals</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Lightning_rod" title="Lightning rod">lightning rod</a> to the public domain.</p>
<p>New NGO communities are starting to use the open-source technology as a tool. One example is the Open Source Youth Network started in 2007 in Lisboa by ISCA members.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open_innovation" title="Open innovation">Open innovation</a> is also a new emerging concept which advocate putting R&amp;D in a common pool. The <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse</a> platform is openly presenting itself as an Open innovation network.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_recreation">Arts and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Arts and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Copyright protection is used in the performing arts and even in athletic activities. Some groups have attempted to remove copyright from such practices.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Russian music composer, scientist and Russian Pirate Party member Victor Argonov presented detailed raw files of his electronic opera "2032"<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> under free license <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons_license" title="Creative Commons license">CC-BY-NC 3.0</a>. This opera was originally composed and published in 2007 by Russian label <a href="/wiki/MC_Entertainment" title="MC Entertainment">MC Entertainment</a> as a commercial product, but then the author changed its status to free. In his blog <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://argonov.livejournal.com">[2]</a> he said that he decided to open raw files (including wav, midi and other used formats) to the public in order to support worldwide pirate actions against <a href="/wiki/SOPA" class="mw-redirect" title="SOPA">SOPA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Personal_Information_Protection_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Personal Information Protection Act">PIPA</a>. Several Internet resources,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> called "2032" the first open-source musical opera in history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_related_movements">Other related movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other related movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/60px-Split-arrows.svg.png" width="60" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/90px-Split-arrows.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/120px-Split-arrows.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="60" data-file-height="20" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article or section <b>may need to be cleaned up or summarized</b> because it has been split from/to <i><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_movement" title="Open-source software movement">Open-source software movement</a></i>.</span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The following are events and applications that have been developed via the open source community, and echo the ideologies of the open source movement.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_e_TnL_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_e_TnL-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/OpenCourseWare" title="OpenCourseWare">Open Education Consortium</a></b>&#160;— an organization composed of various colleges that support open source and share some of their material online. This organization, headed by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, was established to aid in the exchange of open source educational materials.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_e_OEDb_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_e_OEDb-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a></b>&#160;— user-generated <a href="/wiki/Internet_encyclopedia_project" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet encyclopedia project">online encyclopedia</a> with sister projects in academic areas, such as <a href="/wiki/Wikiversity" title="Wikiversity">Wikiversity</a>&#160;— a community dedicated to the creation and exchange of learning materials<sup id="cite_ref-ref_e_Warger_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_e_Warger-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (March 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a></b>&#160;— prior to the existence of <a href="/wiki/Google_Scholar" title="Google Scholar">Google Scholar</a> Beta, this was the first supplier of <a href="/wiki/E-book" title="E-book">electronic books</a> and the very first free library project<sup id="cite_ref-ref_e_Warger_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_e_Warger-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (March 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><b>Synthetic Biology</b>- Synthetic Biology is considered the feasibility of the open source movement. This new technology is important and exciting because it promises to enable cheap, lifesaving new drugs as well as helping to yield biofuels that may help to solve our energy problem. Although synthetic biology has not yet come out of its "lab" stage, it has great potential to become industrialized in the near future. In order to industrialize open source science, there are some scientists who are trying to build their own brand of it.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideologically_related_movements">Ideologically related movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_model&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ideologically related movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Open_access_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open access movement">open access movement</a> is a movement that is similar in ideology to the open source movement. Members of this movement maintain that academic material should be readily available to provide help with “future research, assist in teaching and aid in academic purposes.” The Open access movement aims to eliminate subscription fees and licensing restrictions of academic materials<sup id="cite_ref-ref_a4_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_a4-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Free_culture_movement" title="Free culture movement">free culture movement</a> is a movement that seeks to achieve a culture that engages in collective freedom via freedom of expression, free public access to knowledge and information, full demonstration of creativity and innovation in various arenas and promotion of citizen liberties.<sup id="cite_ref-FreeCulture_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FreeCulture-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> is an organization that “develops, supports, and stewards legal and technical infrastructure that maximizes digital creativity, sharing, and innovation.” It encourages the use of protected properties online for research, education, and creative purposes in pursuit of a universal access. Creative Commons provides an infrastructure through a set of copyright licenses and tools that creates a better balance within the realm of “all rights reserved” properties.<sup id="cite_ref-Creative_Commons_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creative_Commons-94">[94]</a></sup> The Creative Commons license offers a slightly more lenient alternative to “all rights reserved” copyrights for those who do not wish to exclude the use of their material.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Zeitgeist_Movement" title="The Zeitgeist Movement">The Zeitgeist Movement</a> is an international social movement that advocates a transition into a <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a> "resource-based economy" based on <a href="/wiki/Collaboration" title="Collaboration">collaboration</a> in which monetary incentives are replaced by commons-based ones with everyone <a href="/wiki/Sharing_economy" title="Sharing economy">having access</a> to everything (from code to products) as in "open source everything".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> While its activism and events are typically focused on media and education, TZM is a major supporter of open source projects worldwide since they allow for uninhibited advancement of science and technology, independent of constraints posed by institutions of patenting and capitalist investment.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/P2P_Foundation" title="P2P Foundation">P2P Foundation</a> is an “international organization focused on studying, researching, documenting and promoting <a href="/wiki/Social_peer-to-peer_processes" title="Social peer-to-peer processes">peer to peer practices</a> in a very broad sense”. Its objectives incorporate those of the open source movement, whose principles are integrated in a larger socio-economic model.<sup id="cite_ref-P2P_Foundation_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-P2P_Foundation-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
